POEM	For ropes of sand | they would seek to wind,
POEM	And the bottom to dig | from the deepest dale.
POEM	Wiser than all | in counsel I was,
POEM	And there I slept | by the sisters seven,
POEM	And joy full great | did I get from each.
POEM	What, Thor, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	19. "Thjazi I felled, | the giant fierce,
POEM	And I hurled the eyes | of Alvaldi's son
POEM	To the heavens hot above;
POEM	Of my deeds the mightiest | marks are these,
POEM	That all men since can see.
POEM	What, Harbarth, didst thou the while?"
POEM	Harbarth spoke:
POEM	
POEM	20. "Much love-craft I wrought | with them who ride by night,
POEM	When I stole them by stealth from their husbands;
POEM	A giant hard | was Hlebarth, methinks:
POEM	His wand he gave me as gift,
POEM	And I stole his wits away."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	21. "Thou didst repay good gifts with evil mind."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	22. "The oak must have | what it shaves from another;
POEM	In such things each for himself.
POEM	What, Thor, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	23. "Eastward I fared, | of the giants I felled
POEM	Their ill-working women | who went to the mountain;
POEM	And large were the giants' throng | if all were alive;
POEM	No men would there be | in Mithgarth more.
POEM	What, Harbarth, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	24. "In Valland I was, | and wars I raised,
POEM	Princes I angered, | and peace brought never;
POEM	The noble who fall | in the fight hath Othin,
POEM	And Thor hath the race of the thralls."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	25. "Unequal gifts | of men wouldst thou give to the gods,
POEM	If might too much thou shouldst have."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	26. "Thor has might enough, | but never a heart;
POEM	For cowardly fear | in a glove wast thou fain to crawl,
POEM	And there forgot thou wast Thor;
POEM	Afraid there thou wast, | thy fear was such,
POEM	To fart or sneeze | lest Fjalar should hear."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	27. "Thou womanish Harbarth, | to hell would I smite thee straight,
POEM	Could mine arm reach over the sound."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	28. "Wherefore reach over the sound, | since strife we have none?
POEM	What, Thor, didst thou do then?"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	29. "Eastward I was, | and the river I guarded well,
POEM	Where the sons of Svarang | sought me there;
POEM	Stones did they hurl; | small joy did they have of winning;
POEM	Before me there | to ask for peace did they fare.
POEM	What, Harbarth, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	30. "Eastward I was, | and spake with a certain one,
POEM	I played with the linen-white maid, | and met her by stealth;
POEM	I gladdened the gold-decked one, | and she granted me joy."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	31. "Full fair was thy woman-finding."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	32. "Thy help did I need then, Thor, | to hold the white maid fast."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	33. "Gladly, had I been there, | my help to thee had been given."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	34. "I might have trusted thee then, | didst thou not betray thy troth."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	35. "No heel-biter am I, in truth, | like an old leather shoe in spring."
POEM	Harbarth spoke:
POEM	
POEM	36. "What, Thor, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	37. "In Hlesey the brides | of the Berserkers slew I;
POEM	Most evil they were, | and all they betrayed."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	38, "Shame didst thou win, | that women thou slewest, Thor."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	39. "She-wolves they were like, | and women but little;
POEM	My ship, which well | I had trimmed, did they shake;
POEM	With clubs of iron they threatened, | and Thjalfi they drove off.
POEM	What, Harbarth, didst thou the while?"
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	40. "In the host I was | that hither fared,
POEM	The banners to raise, | and the spear to redden."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	41. "Wilt thou now say | that hatred thou soughtest to bring us?"
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	42. "A ring for thy hand | shall make all right for thee,
POEM	As the judge decides | who sets us two at peace."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	43. "Where foundest thou | so foul and scornful a speech?
POEM	More foul a speech | I never before have heard."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	44. "I learned it from men, | the men so old,
POEM	Who dwell in the hills of home."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	45. "A name full good | to heaps of stones thou givest
POEM	When thou callest them hills of home."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	46. "Of such things speak I so."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	47. "Ill for thee comes | thy keenness of tongue,
POEM	If the water I choose to wade;
POEM	Louder, I ween, | than a wolf thou cryest,
POEM	If a blow of my hammer thou hast."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	48. "Sif has a lover at home, | and him shouldst thou meet;
POEM	More fitting it were | on him to put forth thy strength."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	49. "Thy tongue still makes thee say | what seems most ill to me,
POEM	Thou witless man! Thou liest, I ween."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	50. "Truth do I speak, | but slow on thy way thou art;
POEM	Far hadst thou gone | if now in the boat thou hadst fared."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	51. "Thou womanish Harbarth! | here hast thou held me too long."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	52. "I thought not ever | that Asathor would be hindered
POEM	By a ferryman thus from faring."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	53. "One counsel I bring thee now: | row hither thy boat;
POEM	No more of scoffing; | set Magni's father across."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	54. "From the sound go hence; | the passage thou hast not."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	55. "The way now show me, since thou takest me not o'er the water."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	56. "To refuse it is little, to fare it is long;
POEM	A while to the stock, and a while to the stone;
POEM	Then the road to thy left, till Verland thou reachest;
POEM	And there shall Fjorgyn her son Thor find,
POEM	And the road of her children she shows him to Othin's realm."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	57. "May I come so far in a day?"
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	58. "With toil and trouble perchance,
POEM	While the sun still shines, or so I think."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	59. "Short now shall be our speech, for thou speakest in mockery only;
POEM	The passage thou gavest me not I shall pay thee if ever we meet."
POEM	
POEM	Harbarth spake:
POEM	60. "Get hence where every evil thing shall have thee!"
TITLE	HYMISKVITHA
SUBTITLE	The Lay of Hymir
POEM	1. Of old the gods | made feast together,
POEM	And drink they sought | ere sated they were;
POEM	Twigs they shook, | and blood they tried:
POEM	Rich fare in Ægir's | hall they found.
POEM	
POEM	2. The mountain-dweller | sat merry as boyhood,
POEM	But soon like a blinded | man he seemed;
POEM	The son of Ygg | gazed in his eyes:
POEM	For the gods a feast | shalt thou forthwith get.
POEM	
POEM	3. The word-wielder toil | for the giant worked,
POEM	And so revenge | on the gods he sought;
POEM	He bade Sif's mate | the kettle bring:
POEM	Therein for ye all | much ale shall I brew.
POEM	
POEM	4. The far-famed ones | could find it not,
POEM	And the holy gods | could get it nowhere;
POEM	Till in truthful wise | did Tyr speak forth,
POEM	And helpful counsel | to Hlorrithi gave.
POEM	
POEM	5. "There dwells to the east | of Elivagar
POEM	Hymir the wise | at the end of heaven;
POEM	A kettle my father | fierce doth own,
POEM	A mighty vessel | a mile in depth."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	6. "May we win, dost thou think, | this whirler of water?"
POEM	
POEM	Tyr spake:
POEM	Aye, friend, we can, | if cunning we are.
POEM	
POEM	7. Forward that day | with speed they fared,
POEM	From Asgarth came they | to Egil's home;
POEM	The goats with horns | bedecked he guarded;
POEM	Then they sped to the hall | where Hymir dwelt.
POEM	
POEM	8. The youth found his grandam, | that greatly he loathed,
POEM	And full nine hundred | heads she had;
POEM	But the other fair | with gold came forth,
POEM	And the bright-browed one | brought beer to her son.
POEM	
POEM	9. "Kinsman of giants, | beneath the kettle
POEM	Will I set ye both, | ye heroes bold;
POEM	For many a time | my dear-loved mate
POEM	To guests is wrathful | and grim of mind."
POEM	
POEM	10. Late to his home | the misshapen Hymir,
POEM	The giant harsh, | from his hunting came;
POEM	The icicles rattled | as in he came,
POEM	For the fellow's chin-forest | frozen was.
POEM	
POEM	11. "Hail to thee, Hymir! | good thoughts mayst thou have;
POEM	Here has thy son | to thine hall now come;
POEM	(For him have we waited, | his way was long;)
POEM	And with him fares | the foeman of Hroth,
POEM	The friend of mankind, | and Veur they call him.
POEM	
POEM	12. "See where under | the gable they sit!
POEM	Behind the beam | do they hide themselves."
POEM	The beam at the glance | of the giant broke,
POEM	And the mighty pillar | in pieces fell.
POEM	
POEM	13. Eight fell from the ledge, | and one alone,
POEM	The hard-hammered kettle, | of all was whole;
POEM	Forth came they then, | and his foes he sought,
POEM	The giant old, | and held with his eyes.
POEM	
POEM	14. Much sorrow his heart | foretold when he saw
POEM	The giantess' foeman | come forth on the floor;
POEM	Then of the steers | did they bring in three;
POEM	Their flesh to boil | did the giant bid.
POEM	
POEM	15. By a head was each | the shorter hewed,
POEM	And the beasts to the fire | straight they bore;
POEM	The husband of Sif, | ere to sleep he went,
POEM	Alone two oxen | of Hymir's ate.
POEM	
POEM	16. To the comrade hoary | of Hrungnir then
POEM	Did Hlorrithi's meal | full mighty seem;
POEM	Next time at eve | we three must eat
POEM	The food we have | {illegible}s the hunting's spoil.
POEM	
POEM	17. . . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Fain to row on the sea | was Veur, he said,
POEM	If the giant bold | would give him bait.
POEM	
POEM	Hymir spake:
POEM	18. "Go to the herd, | if thou hast it in mind,
POEM	Thou slayer of giants, | thy bait to seek;
POEM	For there thou soon | mayst find, methinks,
POEM	Bait from the oxen | easy to get."
POEM	
POEM	19. Swift to the wood | the hero went,
POEM	Till before him an ox | all black he found;
POEM	From the beast the slayer | of giants broke
POEM	The fortress high | of his double horns.
POEM	
POEM	Hymir spake:
POEM	20. "Thy works, methinks, | are worse by far,
POEM	Thou steerer of ships, | than when still thou sittest."
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	21. The lord of the goats | bade the ape-begotten
POEM	Farther to steer | the steed of the rollers;
POEM	But the giant said | that his will, forsooth,
POEM	Longer to row | was little enough.
POEM	
POEM	22. Two whales on his hook | did the mighty Hymir
POEM	Soon pull up | on a single cast;
POEM	In the stern the kinsman | of Othin sat,
POEM	And Veur with cunning | his cast prepared.
POEM	
POEM	23. The warder of men, | the worm's destroyer,
POEM	Fixed on his hook | the head of the ox;
POEM	There gaped at the bait | the foe of the gods,
POEM	The girdler of all | the earth beneath.
POEM	
POEM	24. The venomous serpent | swiftly up
POEM	To the boat did Thor, | the bold one, pull;
POEM	With his hammer the loathly | hill of the hair
POEM	Of the brother of Fenrir | he smote from above.
POEM	
POEM	25. The monsters roared, | and the rocks resounded,
POEM	And all the earth | so old was shaken;
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Then sank the fish | in the sea forthwith.
POEM	
POEM	26. . . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Joyless as back | they rowed was the giant;
POEM	Speechless did Hymir | sit at the oars,
POEM	With the rudder he sought | a second wind.
POEM	
POEM	Hymir spake:
POEM	27. "The half of our toil | wilt thou have with me,
POEM	And now make fast | our goat of the flood;
POEM	Or home wilt thou bear | the whales to the house,
POEM	Across the gorge | of the wooded glen?"
POEM	
POEM	28. Hlorrithi stood | and the stem he gripped,
POEM	And the sea-horse with water | awash he lifted;
POEM	Oars and bailer | and all he bore
POEM	With the surf-swine home | to the giant's house.
POEM	
POEM	29. His might the giant | again would match,
POEM	For stubborn he was, | with the strength of Thor;
POEM	None truly strong, | though stoutly he rowed,
POEM	Would he call save one | who could break the cup.
POEM	
POEM	30. Hlorrithi then, | when the cup he held,
POEM	Struck with the glass | the pillars of stone;
POEM	As he sat the posts | in pieces he shattered,
POEM	Yet the glass to Hymir whole they brought.
POEM	
POEM	31. But the loved one fair | of the giant found
POEM	A counsel true, | and told her thought:
POEM	Smite the skull of Hymir, | heavy with food,
POEM	For harder it is | than ever was glass.
POEM	
POEM	32. The goats' mighty ruler | then rose on his knee,
POEM	And with all the strength | of a god he struck;
POEM	Whole was the fellow's | helmet-stem,
POEM	But shattered the wine-cup | rounded was.
POEM	
POEM	Hymir spake:
POEM	33. "Fair is the treasure | that from me is gone,
POEM	Since now the cup | on my knees lies shattered;"
POEM	So spake the giant: | "No more can I say
POEM	In days to be, | 'Thou art brewed, mine ale.'
POEM	
POEM	34. "Enough shall it be | if out ye can bring
POEM	Forth from our house | the kettle here."
POEM	Tyr then twice | to move it tried,
POEM	But before him the kettle | twice stood fast.
POEM	
POEM	35. The father of Mothi | the rim seized firm,
POEM	And before it stood | on the floor below;
POEM	Up on his head | Sif's husband raised it,
POEM	And about his heels | the handles clattered.
POEM	
POEM	36. Not long had they fared, | ere backwards looked
POEM	The son of Othin, | once more to see;
POEM	From their caves in the east | beheld he coming
POEM	With Hymir the throng | of the many-headed.
POEM	
POEM	37. He stood and cast | from his back the kettle,
POEM	And Mjollnir, the lover | of murder, he wielded;
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	So all the whales | of the waste he slew.
POEM	
POEM	38. Not long had they fared | ere one there lay
POEM	Of Hlorrithi's goats | half-dead on the ground;
POEM	In his leg the pole-horse | there was lame;
POEM	The deed the evil | Loki had done.
POEM	
POEM	39. But ye all have heard,-- | for of them who have
POEM	The tales of the gods, | who better can tell?
POEM	What prize he won | from the wilderness-dweller,
POEM	Who both his children | gave him to boot.
POEM	
POEM	40. The mighty one came | to the council of gods,
POEM	And the kettle he had | that Hymir's was;
POEM	So gladly their ale | the gods could drink
POEM	In Ægir's hall | at the autumn-time.
TITLE	LOKASENNA
SUBTITLE	Loki's Wrangling
POEM	1. "Speak now, Eldir, | for not one step
POEM	Farther shalt thou fare;
POEM	What ale-talk here | do they have within,
POEM	The sons of the glorious gods?"
POEM	
POEM	Eldir spake:
POEM	2. "Of their weapons they talk, | and their might in war,
POEM	The sons of the glorious gods;
POEM	From the gods and elves | who are gathered here
POEM	No friend in words shalt thou find."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	3. "In shall I go | into Ægir's hall,
POEM	For the feast I fain would see;
POEM	Bale and hatred | I bring to the gods,
POEM	And their mead with venom I mix."
POEM	
POEM	Eldir spake:
POEM	4. "If in thou goest | to Ægir's hall,
POEM	And fain the feast wouldst see,
POEM	And with slander and spite | wouldst sprinkle the gods,
POEM	Think well lest they wipe it on thee."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	5. "Bethink thee, Eldir, | if thou and I
POEM	Shall strive with spiteful speech;
POEM	Richer I grow | in ready words
POEM	If thou speakest too much to me."
POEM	Then Loki went into the hall, but when they who were there saw who had entered, they were all silent.
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	6. "Thirsty I come | into this thine hall,
POEM	I, Lopt, from a journey long,
POEM	To ask of the gods | that one should give
POEM	Fair mead for a drink to me.
POEM	
POEM	7. "Why sit ye silent, | swollen with pride,
POEM	Ye gods, and no answer give?
POEM	At your feast a place | and a seat prepare me,
POEM	Or bid me forth to fare."
POEM	
POEM	Bragi spake:
POEM	8. "A place and a seat | will the gods prepare
POEM	No more in their midst for thee;
POEM	For the gods know well | what men they wish
POEM	To find at their mighty feasts."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	9. "Remember, Othin, | in olden days
POEM	That we both our blood have mixed;
POEM	Then didst thou promise | no ale to pour,
POEM	Unless it were brought for us both."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	10. "Stand forth then, Vithar, | and let the wolf's father
POEM	Find a seat at our feast;
POEM	Lest evil should Loki | speak aloud
POEM	Here within Ægir's hall."
POEM	Then Vithar arose and poured drink for Loki; but before he drank he spoke to the gods:
POEM	
POEM	11. "Hail to you, gods! | ye goddesses, hail!
POEM	Hail to the holy throng!
POEM	Save for the god | who yonder sits,
POEM	Bragi there on the bench."
POEM	
POEM	Bragi spake:
POEM	12. "A horse and a sword | from my hoard will I give,
POEM	And a ring gives Bragi to boot,
POEM	That hatred thou makst not | among the gods;
POEM	So rouse not the great ones to wrath."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	13. "In horses and rings | thou shalt never be rich,
POEM	Bragi, but both shalt thou lack;
POEM	Of the gods and elves | here together met
POEM	Least brave in battle art thou,
POEM	(And shyest thou art of the shot.)"
POEM	
POEM	Bragi spake:
POEM	14. "Now were I without | as I am within,
POEM	And here in Ægir's hall,
POEM	Thine head would I bear | in mine hands away,
POEM	And pay thee the price of thy lies."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	15. "In thy seat art thou bold, | not so are thy deeds,
POEM	Bragi, adorner of benches!
POEM	Go out and fight | if angered thou feelest,
POEM	No hero such forethought has."
POEM	
POEM	Ithun spake:
POEM	16. "Well, prithee, Bragi, | his kinship weigh,
POEM	Since chosen as wish-son he was;
POEM	And speak not to Loki | such words of spite
POEM	Here within Ægir's hall."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	17. "Be silent, Ithun! | thou art, I say,
POEM	Of women most lustful in love,
POEM	Since thou thy washed-bright | arms didst wind
POEM	About thy brother's slayer."
POEM	
POEM	Ithun spake:
POEM	18. "To Loki I speak not | with spiteful words
POEM	Here within Ægir's hall;
POEM	And Bragi I calm, | who is hot with beer,
POEM	For I wish not that fierce they should fight."
POEM	
POEM	Gefjun spake:
POEM	19. "Why, ye gods twain, | with bitter tongues
POEM	Raise hate among us here?
POEM	Loki is famed | for his mockery foul,
POEM	And the dwellers in heaven he hates."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	20. "Be silent, Gefjun! | for now shall I say
POEM	Who led thee to evil life;
POEM	The boy so fair | gave a necklace bright,
POEM	And about him thy leg was laid."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	21. "Mad art thou, Loki, | and little of wit,
POEM	The wrath of Gefjun to rouse;
POEM	For the fate that is set | for all she sees,
POEM	Even as I, methinks."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	22. "Be silent, Othin! | not justly thou settest
POEM	The fate of the fight among men;
POEM	Oft gavst thou to him | who deserved not the gift,
POEM	To the baser, the battle's prize."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	23. "Though I gave to him | who deserved not the gift,
POEM	To the baser, the battle's prize;
POEM	Winters eight | wast thou under the earth,
POEM	Milking the cows as a maid,
POEM	(Ay, and babes didst thou bear;
POEM	Unmanly thy soul must seem.)"
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	24. "They say that with spells | in Samsey once
POEM	Like witches with charms didst thou work;
POEM	And in witch's guise | among men didst thou go;
POEM	Unmanly thy soul must seem."
POEM	
POEM	Frigg spake:
POEM	25. "Of the deeds ye two | of old have done
POEM	Ye should make no speech among men;
POEM	Whate'er ye have done | in days gone by,
POEM	Old tales should ne'er be told."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	26. "Be silent, Frigg! | thou art Fjorgyn's wife,
POEM	But ever lustful in love;
POEM	For Vili and Ve, | thou wife of Vithrir,
POEM	Both in thy bosom have lain."
POEM	
POEM	Frigg spake:
POEM	27. "If a son like Baldr | were by me now,
POEM	Here within Ægir's hall,
POEM	From the sons of the gods | thou shouldst go not forth
POEM	Till thy fierceness in fight were tried."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	28. "Thou wilt then, Frigg, | that further I tell
POEM	Of the ill that now I know;
POEM	Mine is the blame | that Baldr no more
POEM	Thou seest ride home to the hall."
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	29. "Mad art thou, Loki, | that known thou makest
POEM	The wrong and shame thou hast wrought;
POEM	The fate of all | does Frigg know well,
POEM	Though herself she says it not."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	30. "Be silent, Freyja! | for fully I know thee,
POEM	Sinless thou art not thyself;
POEM	Of the gods and elves | who are gathered here,
POEM	Each one as thy lover has lain."
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	31. "False is thy tongue, | and soon shalt thou find
POEM	That it sings thee an evil song;
POEM	The gods are wroth, | and the goddesses all,
POEM	And in grief shalt thou homeward go."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	32. "Be silent, Freyja! | thou foulest witch,
POEM	And steeped full sore in sin;
POEM	In the arms of thy brother | the bright gods caught thee
POEM	When Freyja her wind set free."
POEM	
POEM	Njorth spake:
POEM	33. "Small ill does it work | though a woman may have
POEM	A lord or a lover or both;
POEM	But a wonder it is | that this womanish god
POEM	Comes hither, though babes he has borne."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	34. "Be silent, Njorth; | thou wast eastward sent,
POEM	To the gods as a hostage given;
POEM	And the daughters of Hymir | their privy had
POEM	When use did they make of thy mouth."
POEM	
POEM	Njorth spake:
POEM	35. "Great was my gain, | though long was I gone,
POEM	To the gods as a hostage given;
POEM	The son did I have | whom no man hates,
POEM	And foremost of gods is found."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	36. "Give heed now, Njorth, | nor boast too high,
POEM	No longer I hold it hid;
POEM	With thy sister hadst thou | so fair a son,
POEM	Thus hadst thou no worse a hope."
POEM	
POEM	Tyr spake:
POEM	37. "Of the heroes brave | is Freyr the best
POEM	Here in the home of the gods;
POEM	He harms not maids | nor the wives of men,
POEM	And the bound from their fetters he frees."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	38. "Be silent, Tyr! | for between two men
POEM	Friendship thou ne'er couldst fashion;
POEM	Fain would I tell | how Fenrir once
POEM	Thy right hand rent from thee."
POEM	
POEM	Tyr spake:
POEM	39. "My hand do I lack, | but Hrothvitnir thou,
POEM	And the loss brings longing to both;
POEM	Ill fares the wolf | who shall ever await
POEM	In fetters the fall of the gods."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	40. "Be silent, Tyr! | for a son with me
POEM	Thy wife once chanced to win;
POEM	Not a penny, methinks, | wast thou paid for the wrong,
POEM	Nor wast righted an inch, poor wretch."
POEM	
POEM	Freyr spake:
POEM	41. "By the mouth of the river | the wolf remains
POEM	Till the gods to destruction go;
POEM	Thou too shalt soon, | if thy tongue is not stilled,
POEM	Be fettered, thou forger of ill."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	42. "The daughter of Gymir | with gold didst thou buy,
POEM	And sold thy sword to boot;
POEM	But when Muspell's sons | through Myrkwood ride,
POEM	Thou shalt weaponless wait, poor wretch."
POEM	
POEM	Byggvir spake:
POEM	43. "Had I birth so famous | as Ingunar-Freyr,
POEM	And sat in so lofty a seat,
POEM	I would crush to marrow | this croaker of ill,
POEM	And beat all his body to bits."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	44. "What little creature | goes crawling there,
POEM	Snuffling and snapping about?
POEM	At Freyr's ears ever | wilt thou be found,
POEM	Or muttering hard at the mill."
POEM	
POEM	Byggvir spake:
POEM	45. "Byggvir my name, | and nimble am I,
POEM	As gods and men do grant;
POEM	And here am I proud | that the children of Hropt
POEM	Together all drink ale."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	46. "Be silent, Byggvir! | thou never couldst set
POEM	Their shares of the meat for men;
POEM	Hid in straw on the floor, | they found thee not
POEM	When heroes were fain to fight."
POEM	
POEM	Heimdall spake:
POEM	47. "Drunk art thou, Loki, | and mad are thy deeds,
POEM	Why, Loki, leavst thou this not?
POEM	For drink beyond measure | will lead all men
POEM	No thought of their tongues to take."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	48. "Be silent, Heimdall! | in days long since
POEM	Was an evil fate for thee fixed;
POEM	With back held stiff | must thou ever stand,
POEM	As warder of heaven to watch."
POEM	
POEM	Skathi spake:
POEM	49. "Light art thou, Loki, | but longer thou mayst not
POEM	In freedom flourish thy tail;
POEM	On the rocks the gods bind thee | with bowels torn
POEM	Forth from thy frost-cold son."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	50. "Though on rocks the gods bind me | with bowels torn
POEM	Forth from my frost-cold son,
POEM	I was first and last | at the deadly fight
POEM	There where Thjazi we caught."
POEM	
POEM	Skathi spake:
POEM	51. "Wert thou first and last | at the deadly fight
POEM	There where Thjazi was caught,
POEM	From my dwellings and fields | shall ever come forth
POEM	A counsel cold for thee."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	52. "More lightly thou spakest | with Laufey's son,
POEM	When thou badst me come to thy bed;
POEM	Such things must be known | if now we two
POEM	Shall seek our sins to tell."
POEM	Then Sif came forward and poured mead for Loki in a crystal cup, and said:
POEM	
POEM	53. "Hail too thee, Loki, | and take thou here
POEM	The crystal cup of old mead;
POEM	For me at least, | alone of the gods,
POEM	Blameless thou knowest to be."
POEM	He took the horn, and drank therefrom:
POEM	
POEM	54. "Alone thou wert | if truly thou wouldst
POEM	All men so shyly shun;
POEM	But one do I know | full well, methinks,
POEM	Who had thee from Hlorrithi's arms,--
POEM	(Loki the crafty in lies.)"
POEM	
POEM	Beyla spake:
POEM	55. "The mountains shake, | and surely I think
POEM	From his home comes Hlorrithi now;
POEM	He will silence the man | who is slandering here
POEM	Together both gods and men."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	56. "Be silent, Beyla! | thou art Byggvir's wife,
POEM	And deep art thou steeped in sin;
POEM	A greater shame | to the gods came ne'er,
POEM	Befouled thou art with thy filth."
POEM	
POEM	Then came Thor forth, and spake:
POEM	57. "Unmanly one, cease, | or the mighty hammer,
POEM	Mjollnir, shall close thy mouth;
POEM	Thy shoulder-cliff | shall I cleave from thy neck,
POEM	And so shall thy life be lost."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	58. "Lo, in has come | the son of Earth:
POEM	Why threaten so loudly, Thor?
POEM	Less fierce thou shalt go | to fight with the wolf
POEM	When he swallows Sigfather up."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	59. "Unmanly one, cease, | or the mighty hammer,
POEM	Mjollnir, shall close thy mouth;
POEM	I shall hurl thee up | and out in the East,
POEM	Where men shall see thee no more."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	60. "That thou hast fared | on the East-road forth
POEM	To men shouldst thou say no more;
POEM	In the thumb of a glove | didst thou hide, thou great one,
POEM	And there forgot thou wast Thor."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	61. "Unmanly one, cease, | or the mighty hammer,
POEM	Mjollnir, shall close thy mouth;
POEM	My right hand shall smite thee | with Hrungnir's slayer,
POEM	Till all thy bones are broken."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	62. "Along time still | do I think to live,
POEM	Though thou threatenest thus with thy hammer;
POEM	Rough seemed the straps | of Skrymir's wallet,
POEM	When thy meat thou mightest not get,
POEM	(And faint from hunger didst feel.)"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	63. "Unmanly one, cease, | or the mighty hammer,
POEM	Mjollnir, shall close thy mouth;
POEM	The slayer of Hrungnir | shall send thee to hell,
POEM	And down to the gate of death."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	64. "'1 have said to the gods | and the sons of the god,
POEM	The things that whetted my thoughts;
POEM	But before thee alone | do I now go forth,
POEM	For thou fightest well, I ween.
POEM	
POEM	65. "Ale hast thou brewed, | but, Ægir, now
POEM	Such feasts shalt thou make no more;
POEM	O'er all that thou hast | which is here within
POEM	Shall play the flickering flames,
POEM	(And thy back shall be burnt with fire.)"
POEM	And after that Loki hid himself in Franang's waterfall in the guise of a salmon, and there the gods took
POEM	him. He was bound with the bowels of his son Vali, but his son Narfi was changed to a wolf. Skathi took
POEM	a poison-snake and fastened it up over Loki's face, and the poison dropped thereon. Sigyn, Loki's wife,
POEM	sat there and held a shell under the poison, but when the shell was full she bore away the poison, and
POEM	meanwhile the poison dropped on Loki. Then he struggled so hard that the whole earth shook therewith;
POEM	and now that is called an earthquake.
TITLE	THRYMSKVITHA
SUBTITLE	The Lay of Thrym
POEM	1. Wild was Vingthor | when he awoke,
POEM	And when his mighty | hammer he missed;
POEM	He shook his beard, | his hair was bristling,
POEM	As the son of Jorth | about him sought.
POEM	
POEM	2. Hear now the speech | that first he spake:
POEM	Harken, Loki, | and heed my words,
POEM	Nowhere on earth | is it known to man,
POEM	Nor in heaven above: | our hammer is stolen.
POEM	
POEM	3. To the dwelling fair | of Freyja went they,
POEM	
POEM	Hear now the speech | that first he spake:
POEM	Wilt thou, Freyja, | thy feather-dress lend me,
POEM	That so my hammer | I may seek?
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	4. "Thine should it be | though of silver bright,
POEM	And I would give it | though 'twere of gold."
POEM	Then Loki flew, | and the feather-dress whirred,
POEM	Till he left behind him | the home of the gods,
POEM	And reached at last | the realm of the giants.
POEM	
POEM	5. Thrym sat on a mound, | the giants' master,
POEM	Leashes of gold | he laid for his dogs,
POEM	And stroked and smoothed | the manes of his steeds.
POEM	
POEM	Thrym spake:
POEM	6. "How fare the gods, | how fare the elves?
POEM	Why comst thou alone | to the giants' land?"
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	III fare the gods, | ill fare the elves!
POEM	Hast thou hidden | Hlorrithi's hammer?
POEM	
POEM	Thrym spake:
POEM	7. "I have hidden | Hlorrithi's hammer,
POEM	Eight miles down | deep in the earth;
POEM	And back again | shall no man bring it
POEM	If Freyja I win not | to be my wife."
POEM	
POEM	8. Then Loki flew, | and the feather-dress whirred,
POEM	Till he left behind him | the home of the giants,
POEM	And reached at last | the realm of the gods.
POEM	There in the courtyard | Thor he met:
POEM	
POEM	Hear now the speech | that first he spake:
POEM	9. "Hast thou found tidings | as well as trouble?
POEM	Thy news in the air | shalt thou utter now;
POEM	Oft doth the sitter | his story forget,
POEM	And lies he speaks | who lays himself down."
POEM	
POEM	Loki spake:
POEM	I0. "Trouble I have, | and tidings as well:
POEM	Thrym, king of the giants, | keeps thy hammer,
POEM	And back again | shall no man bring it
POEM	If Freyja he wins not | to be his wife."
POEM	
POEM	11. Freyja the fair | then went they to find
POEM	
POEM	Hear now the speech | that first he spake:
POEM	Bind on, Freyja, | the bridal veil,
POEM	For we two must haste | to the giants' home.
POEM	
POEM	12. Wrathful was Freyja, | and fiercely she snorted,
POEM	And the dwelling great | of the gods was shaken,
POEM	And burst was the mighty | Brisings' necklace:
POEM	Most lustful indeed | should I look to all
POEM	If I journeyed with thee | to the giants' home.
POEM	
POEM	13. Then were the gods | together met,
POEM	And the goddesses came | and council held,
POEM	And the far-famed ones | a plan would find,
POEM	How they might Hlorrithi's | hammer win.
POEM	
POEM	14. Then Heimdall spake, | whitest of the gods,
POEM	Like the Wanes he knew | the future well:
POEM	Bind we on Thor | the bridal veil,
POEM	Let him bear the mighty | Brisings' necklace;
POEM	
POEM	15. Keys around him | let there rattle,
POEM	And down to his knees | hang woman's dress;
POEM	With gems full broad | upon his breast,
POEM	And a pretty cap | to crown his head."
POEM	
POEM	16. Then Thor the mighty | his answer made:
POEM	Me would the gods | unmanly call
POEM	If I let bind | the bridal veil.
POEM	
POEM	17. Then Loki spake, | the son of Laufey:
POEM	Be silent, Thor, | and speak not thus;
POEM	Else will the giants | in Asgarth dwell
POEM	If thy hammer is brought not | home to thee.
POEM	
POEM	8. Then bound they on Thor | the bridal veil,
POEM	And next the mighty | Brisings' necklace.
POEM	
POEM	19. Keys around him | let they rattle,
POEM	And down to his knees | hung woman's dress;
POEM	With gems full broad | upon his breast,
POEM	And a pretty cap | to crown his head.
POEM	
POEM	20. Then Loki spake, | the son of Laufey:
POEM	As thy maid-servant thither | I go with thee;
POEM	We two shall haste | to the giants' home.
POEM	
POEM	21. Then home the goats | to the hall were driven,
POEM	They wrenched at the halters, | swift were they to run;
POEM	The mountains burst, | earth burned with fire,
POEM	And Othin's son | sought Jotunheim.
POEM	
POEM	22. Then loud spake Thrym, | the giants' leader:
POEM	Bestir ye, giants, | put straw on the benches;
POEM	Now Freyja they bring | to be my bride,
POEM	The daughter of Njorth | out of Noatun.
POEM	
POEM	23. Gold-horned cattle | go to my stables,
POEM	Jet-black oxen, | the giant's joy;
POEM	Many my gems, | and many my jewels,
POEM	Freyja alone | did I lack, methinks."
POEM	
POEM	24. Early it was | to evening come,
POEM	And forth was borne | the beer for the giants;
POEM	Thor alone ate an ox, | and eight salmon,
POEM	All the dainties as well | that were set for the women;
POEM	And drank Sif's mate | three tuns of mead.
POEM	
POEM	25. Then loud spake Thrym, | the giants' leader:
POEM	Who ever saw bride | more keenly bite?
POEM	I ne'er saw bride | with a broader bite,
POEM	Nor a maiden who drank | more mead than this!
POEM	
POEM	26. Hard by there sat | the serving-maid wise,
POEM	So well she answered | the giant's words:
POEM	From food has Freyja | eight nights fasted,
POEM	So hot was her longing | for Jotunheim.
POEM	
POEM	27. Thrym looked 'neath the veil, | for he longed to kiss,
POEM	But back he leaped | the length of the hall:
POEM	Why are so fearful | the eyes of Freyja?
POEM	Fire, methinks, | from her eyes burns forth.
POEM	
POEM	28. Hard by there sat | the serving-maid wise,
POEM	So well she answered | the giant's words:
POEM	No sleep has Freyja | for eight nights found,
POEM	So hot was her longing | for Jotunheim.
POEM	
POEM	29. Soon came the giant's | luckless sister,
POEM	Who feared not to ask | the bridal fee:
POEM	From thy hands the rings | of red gold take,
POEM	If thou wouldst win | my willing love,
POEM	(My willing love | and welcome glad.)
POEM	
POEM	30: Then loud spake Thrym, | the giants' leader:
POEM	Bring in the hammer | to hallow the bride;
POEM	On the maiden's knees | let Mjollnir lie,
POEM	That us both the band | of Vor may bless.
POEM	
POEM	31. The heart in the breast | of Hlorrithi laughed
POEM	When the hard-souled one | his hammer beheld;
POEM	First Thrym, the king | of the giants, he killed,
POEM	Then all the folk | of the giants he felled.
POEM	
POEM	32. The giant's sister | old he slew,
POEM	She who had begged | the bridal fee;
POEM	A stroke she got | in the shilling's stead,
POEM	And for many rings | the might of the hammer.
POEM	
POEM	33. And so his hammer | got Othin's son.
TITLE	ALVISSMOL
SUBTITLE	The Ballad of Alvis
POEM	1. "Now shall the bride | my benches adorn,
POEM	And homeward haste forthwith;
POEM	Eager for wedlock | to all shall I seem,
POEM	Nor at home shall they rob me of rest."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	2. "What, pray, art thou? | Why so pale round the nose?
POEM	By the dead hast thou lain of late?
POEM	To a giant like | dost thou look, methinks;
POEM	Thou wast not born for the bride."
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	3. "Alvis am I, | and under the earth
POEM	My home 'neath the rocks I have;
POEM	With the wagon-guider | a word do I seek,
POEM	Let the gods their bond not break."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	4. "Break it shall I, | for over the bride
POEM	Her father has foremost right;
POEM	At home was I not | when the promise thou hadst,
POEM	And I give her alone of the gods."
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	5. "What hero claims | such right to hold
POEM	O'er the bride that shines so bright?
POEM	Not many will know thee, | thou wandering man!
POEM	Who was bought with rings to bear thee?"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	6. "Vingthor, the wanderer | wide, am I,
POEM	And I am Sithgrani's son;
POEM	Against my will | shalt thou get the maid,
POEM	And win the marriage word."
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	7. "Thy good-will now | shall I quickly get,
POEM	And win the marriage word;
POEM	I long to have, | and I would not lack,
POEM	This snow-white maid for mine."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	8. "The love of the maid | I may not keep thee
POEM	From winning, thou guest so wise,
POEM	If of every world | thou canst tell me all
POEM	That now I wish to know.
POEM	
POEM	9. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the earth, | that lies before all,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	10. " 'Earth' to men, 'Field' | to the gods it is,
POEM	The Ways' is it called by the Wanes;
POEM	Ever Green' by the giants, | 'The Grower' by elves,
POEM	The Moist' by the holy ones high."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	11. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the heaven, | beheld of the high one,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	12. " 'Heaven' men call it, | 'The Height' the gods,
POEM	The Wanes 'The Weaver of Winds';
POEM	Giants 'The Up-World,' | elves 'The Fair-Roof,'
POEM	The dwarfs 'The Dripping Hall.'"
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	13. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men.:
POEM	What call they the moon, | that men behold,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	14. "'Moon' with men, 'Flame' | the gods among,
POEM	The Wheel' in the house of hell;
POEM	The Goer' the giants, | 'The Gleamer' the dwarfs,
POEM	The elves 'The Teller of Time."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	15. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the sun, | that all men see,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	16. "Men call it 'Sun,' | gods 'Orb of the Sun,'
POEM	The Deceiver of Dvalin' the dwarfs;
POEM	The giants 'The Ever-Bright,' | elves 'Fair Wheel,'
POEM	All-Glowing' the sons of the gods."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	17. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the clouds, | that keep the rains,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	18. "'Clouds' men name them, | 'Rain-Hope' gods call them,
POEM	The Wanes call them 'Kites of the Wind';
POEM	Water-Hope' giants, | 'Weather-Might' elves,
POEM	The Helmet of Secrets' in hell."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	19. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the wind, | that widest fares,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	20. "'Wind' do men call it, | the gods 'The Waverer,'
POEM	The Neigher' the holy ones high;
POEM	The Wailer' the giants, | 'Roaring Wender' the elves,
POEM	In hell 'The Blustering Blast.'
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	21. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the calm, | that quiet lies,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	22. " 'Calm' men call it, | 'The Quiet' the gods,
POEM	The Wanes 'The Hush of the Winds';
POEM	The Sultry' the giants, | elves 'Day's Stillness,'
POEM	The dwarfs 'The Shelter of Day.'
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	23. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the sea, | whereon men sail,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	24. " 'Sea' men call it, | gods 'The Smooth-Lying,'
POEM	The Wave' is it called by the Wanes;
POEM	Eel-Home' the giants, | 'Drink-Stuff' the elves,
POEM	For the dwarfs its name is 'The Deep.'
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	25. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the fire, | that flames for men,
POEM	In each of all the worlds?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	26. " 'Fire' men call it, | and 'Flame' the gods,
POEM	By the Wanes is it 'Wildfire' called;
POEM	The Biter' by giants, | 'The Burner' by dwarfs,
POEM	The Swift' in the house of hell."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	27. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the wood, | that grows for mankind,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	28. "Men call it 'The Wood, | gods 'The Mane of the Field,'
POEM	Seaweed of Hills' in hell;
POEM	Flame-Food' the giants, | 'Fair-Limbed' the elves,
POEM	The Wand' is it called by the Wanes."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	29. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the night, | the daughter of Nor,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	30. "'Night' men call it, | 'Darkness' gods name it,
POEM	The Hood' the holy ones high;
POEM	The giants 'The Lightless,' | the elves 'Sleep's joy"
POEM	The dwarfs 'The Weaver of Dreams."'
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	31. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the seed, | that is sown by men,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	32. "Men call it 'Grain,' | and 'Corn' the gods,
POEM	Growth' in the world of the Wanes;
POEM	The Eaten' by giants, | 'Drink-Stuff' by elves,
POEM	In hell 'The Slender Stem.'
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	33. "Answer me, Alvis! | thou knowest all,
POEM	Dwarf, of the doom of men:
POEM	What call they the ale, | that is quaffed of men,
POEM	In each and every world?"
POEM	
POEM	Alvis spake:
POEM	34. "'Ale' among men, | 'Beer' the gods among,
POEM	In the world of the Wanes 'The Foaming';
POEM	Bright Draught' with giants, | 'Mead' with dwellers in hell,
POEM	The Feast-Draught' with Suttung's sons."
POEM	
POEM	Thor spake:
POEM	.3.5. "In a single breast | I never have seen
POEM	More wealth of wisdom old;
POEM	But with treacherous wiles | must I now betray thee:
POEM	The day has caught thee, dwarf!
POEM	(Now the sun shines here in the hall.)"
TITLE	BALDRS DRAUMAR
SUBTITLE	Baldr's Dreams
POEM	1. Once were the gods | together met,
POEM	And the goddesses came | and council held,
POEM	And the far-famed ones | the truth would find,
POEM	Why baleful dreams | to Baldr had come.
POEM	
POEM	2. Then Othin rose, | the enchanter old,
POEM	And the saddle he laid | on Sleipnir's back;
POEM	Thence rode he down | to Niflhel deep,
POEM	And the hound he met | that came from hell.
POEM	
POEM	3. Bloody he was | on his breast before,
POEM	At the father of magic | he howled from afar;
POEM	Forward rode Othin, | the earth resounded
POEM	Till the house so high | of Hel he reached.
POEM	
POEM	4. Then Othin rode | to the eastern door,
POEM	There, he knew well, | was the wise-woman's grave;
POEM	Magic he spoke | and mighty charms,
POEM	Till spell-bound she rose, | and in death she spoke:
POEM	
POEM	5. "What is the man, | to me unknown,
POEM	That has made me travel | the troublous road?
POEM	I was snowed on with snow, | and smitten with rain,
POEM	And drenched with dew; | long was I dead."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	6. "Vegtam my name, | I am Valtam's son;
POEM	Speak thou of hell, | for of heaven I know:
POEM	For whom are the benches | bright with rings,
POEM	And the platforms gay | bedecked with gold?"
POEM	
POEM	The Wise-Woman spake:
POEM	7. "Here for Baldr | the mead is brewed,
POEM	The shining drink, | and a shield lies o'er it;
POEM	But their hope is gone | from the mighty gods.
POEM	Unwilling I spake, | and now would be still."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	8. "Wise-woman, cease not! | I seek from thee
POEM	All to know | that I fain would ask:
POEM	Who shall the bane | of Baldr become,
POEM	And steal the life | from Othin's son?"
POEM	
POEM	The Wise-Woman spake:
POEM	9. "Hoth thither bears | the far-famed branch,
POEM	He shall the bane | of Baldr become,
POEM	And steal the life | from Othin's son.
POEM	Unwilling I spake, | and now would be still."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	10. "Wise-woman, cease not! | I seek from thee
POEM	All to know | that I fain would ask:
POEM	Who shall vengeance win | for the evil work,
POEM	Or bring to the flames | the slayer of Baldr?"
POEM	
POEM	The Wise-Woman spake:
POEM	11. "Rind bears Vali | in Vestrsalir,
POEM	And one night old | fights Othin's son;
POEM	His hands he shall wash not, | his hair he shall comb not,
POEM	Till the slayer of Baldr | he brings to the flames.
POEM	Unwilling I spake, | and now would be still."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	12. "Wise-woman, cease not! | I seek from thee
POEM	All to know | that I fain would ask:
POEM	What maidens are they | who then shall weep,
POEM	And toss to the sky | the yards of the sails?"
POEM	
POEM	The Wise-Woman spake:
POEM	13. "Vegtam thou art not, | as erstwhile I thought;
POEM	Othin thou art, | the enchanter old."
POEM	
POEM	Othin spake:
POEM	No wise-woman art thou, | nor wisdom hast;
POEM	Of giants three | the mother art thou.
POEM	
POEM	The Wise-Woman spake:
POEM	14. "Home ride, Othin, | be ever proud;
POEM	For no one of men | shall seek me more
POEM	Till Loki wanders | loose from his bonds,
POEM	And to the last strife | the destroyers come."
TITLE	RIGSTHULA
SUBTITLE	The Song of Rig
POEM	1. Men say there went | by ways so green
POEM	Of old the god, | the aged and wise,
POEM	Mighty and strong | did Rig go striding.
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	2. Forward he went | on the midmost way,
POEM	He came to a dwelling, | a door on its posts;
POEM	In did he fare, | on the floor was a fire,
POEM	Two hoary ones | by the hearth there sat,
POEM	Ai and Edda, | in olden dress.
POEM	
POEM	3. Rig knew well | wise words to speak,
POEM	Soon in the midst | of the room he sat,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	4. A loaf of bread | did Edda bring,
POEM	Heavy and thick | and swollen with husks;
POEM	Forth on the table | she set the fare,
POEM	And broth for the meal | in a bowl there was.
POEM	(Calf's flesh boiled | was the best of the dainties.)
POEM	
POEM	5. Rig knew well | wise words to speak,
POEM	Thence did he rise, | made ready to sleep;
POEM	Soon in the bed | himself did he lay,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	6. Thus was he there | for three nights long,
POEM	Then forward he went | on the midmost way,
POEM	And so nine months | were soon passed by.
POEM	
POEM	7. A son bore Edda, | with water they sprinkled him,
POEM	With a cloth his hair | so black they covered;
POEM	Thræll they named him, | . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	8. The skin was wrinkled | and rough on his hands,
POEM	Knotted his knuckles, | . . . . .
POEM	Thick his fingers, | and ugly his face,
POEM	Twisted his back, | and big his heels.
POEM	
POEM	9. He began to grow, | and to gain in strength,
POEM	Soon of his might | good use he made;
POEM	With bast he bound, | and burdens carried,
POEM	Home bore faggots | the whole day long.
POEM	
POEM	10. One came to their home, | crooked her legs,
POEM	Stained were her feet, | and sunburned her arms,
POEM	Flat was her nose; | her name was Thir.
POEM	
POEM	11. Soon in the midst | of the room she sat,
POEM	By her side there sat | the son of the house;
POEM	They whispered both, | and the bed made ready,
POEM	Thræll and Thir, | till the day was through.
POEM	
POEM	12. Children they had, | they lived and were happy,
POEM	Fjosnir and Klur | they were called, methinks,
POEM	Hreim and Kleggi, | Kefsir, Fulnir,
POEM	Drumb, Digraldi, | Drott and Leggjaldi,
POEM	Lut and Hosvir; | the house they cared for,
POEM	Ground they dunged, | and swine they guarded,
POEM	Goats they tended, | and turf they dug.
POEM	
POEM	13. Daughters had they, | Drumba and Kumba,
POEM	Ökkvinkalfa, | Arinnefla,
POEM	Ysja and Ambott, | Eikintjasna,
POEM	Totrughypja | and Tronubeina;
POEM	And thence has risen | the race of thralls.
POEM	
POEM	14. Forward went Rig, | his road was straight,
POEM	To a hall he came, | and a door there hung;
POEM	In did he fare, | on the floor was a fire:
POEM	Afi and Amma | owned the house.
POEM	
POEM	15. There sat the twain, | and worked at their tasks:
POEM	The man hewed wood | for the weaver's beam;
POEM	His beard was trimmed, | o'er his brow a curl,
POEM	His clothes fitted close; | in the corner a chest.
POEM	
POEM	16. The woman sat | and the distaff wielded,
POEM	At the weaving with arms | outstretched she worked;
POEM	On her head was a band, | on her breast a smock;
POEM	On her shoulders a kerchief | with clasps there was.
POEM	
POEM	17. Rig knew well | wise words to speak,
POEM	Soon in the midst | of the room he sat,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	18. Then took Amma | . . . . .
POEM	The vessels full | with the fare she set,
POEM	Calf's flesh boiled | was the best of the dainties.
POEM	
POEM	19. Rig knew well | wise words to speak,
POEM	He rose from the board, | made ready to sleep;
POEM	Soon in the bed | himself did he lay,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	20. Thus was he there | for three nights long,
POEM	Then forward he went | on the midmost way,
POEM	And so nine months | were soon passed by.
POEM	
POEM	21. A son bore Amma, | with water they sprinkled him,
POEM	Karl they named him; | in a cloth she wrapped him,
POEM	He was ruddy of face, | and flashing his eyes.
POEM	
POEM	22. He began to grow, | and to gain in strength,
POEM	Oxen he ruled, | and plows made ready,
POEM	Houses he built, | and barns he fashioned,
POEM	Carts he made, | and the plow he managed.
POEM	
POEM	23. Home did they bring | the bride for Karl,
POEM	In goatskins clad, | and keys she bore;
POEM	Snör was her name, | 'neath the veil she sat;
POEM	A home they made ready, | and rings exchanged,
POEM	The bed they decked, | and a dwelling made.
POEM	
POEM	24. Sons they had, | they lived and were happy:
POEM	Hal and Dreng, | Holth, Thegn and Smith,
POEM	Breith and Bondi, | Bundinskeggi,
POEM	Bui and Boddi, | Brattskegg and Segg.
POEM	
POEM	25. Daughters they had, | and their names are here:
POEM	Snot, Bruth, Svanni, | Svarri, Sprakki,
POEM	Fljoth, Sprund and Vif, | Feima, Ristil:
POEM	And thence has risen | the yeomen's race.
POEM	
POEM	26. Thence went Rig, | his road was straight,
POEM	A hall he saw, | the doors faced south;
POEM	The portal stood wide, | on the posts was a ring,
POEM	Then in he fared; | the floor was strewn.
POEM	
POEM	27. Within two gazed | in each other's eyes,
POEM	Fathir and Mothir, | and played with their fingers;
POEM	There sat the house-lord, | wound strings for the bow,
POEM	Shafts he fashioned, | and bows he shaped.
POEM	
POEM	28. The lady sat, | at her arms she looked,
POEM	She smoothed the cloth, | and fitted the sleeves;
POEM	Gay was her cap, | on her breast were clasps,
POEM	Broad was her train, | of blue was her gown,
POEM	Her brows were bright, | her breast was shining,
POEM	Whiter her neck | than new-fallen snow.
POEM	
POEM	29. Rig knew | well wise words to speak,
POEM	Soon in the midst | of the room he sat,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	30. Then Mothir brought | a broidered cloth,
POEM	Of linen bright, | and the board she covered;
POEM	And then she took | the loaves so thin,
POEM	And laid them, white | from the wheat, on the cloth.
POEM	
POEM	31. Then forth she brought | the vessels full,
POEM	With silver covered, | and set before them,
POEM	Meat all browned, | and well-cooked birds;
POEM	In the pitcher was wine, | of plate were the cups,
POEM	So drank they and talked | till the day was gone.
POEM	
POEM	32. Rig knew well | wise words to speak,
POEM	Soon did he rise, | made ready to sleep;
POEM	So in the bed | himself did he lay,
POEM	And on either side | the others were.
POEM	
POEM	33. Thus was he there | for three nights long,
POEM	Then forward he went | on the midmost way,
POEM	And so nine months | were soon passed by.
POEM	
POEM	34. A son had Mothir, | in silk they wrapped him,
POEM	With water they sprinkled him, | Jarl he was;
POEM	Blond was his hair, | and bright his cheeks,
POEM	Grim as a snake's | were his glowing eyes.
POEM	
POEM	35. To grow in the house | did Jarl begin,
POEM	Shields he brandished, | and bow-strings wound,
POEM	Bows he shot, | and shafts he fashioned,
POEM	Arrows he loosened, | and lances wielded,
POEM	Horses he rode, | and hounds unleashed,
POEM	Swords he handled, | and sounds he swam.
POEM	
POEM	36. Straight from the grove | came striding Rig,
POEM	Rig came striding, | and runes he taught him;
POEM	By his name he called him, | as son he claimed him,
POEM	And bade him hold | his heritage wide,
POEM	His heritage wide, | the ancient homes.
POEM	
POEM	37. . . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Forward he rode | through the forest dark,
POEM	O'er the frosty crags, | till a hall he found.
POEM	
POEM	38. His spear he shook, | his shield he brandished,
POEM	His horse he spurred, | with his sword he hewed;
POEM	Wars he raised, | and reddened the field,
POEM	Warriors slew he, | and land he won.
POEM	
POEM	39. Eighteen halls | ere long did he hold,
POEM	Wealth did he get, | and gave to all,
POEM	Stones and jewels | and slim-flanked steeds,
POEM	Rings he offered, | and arm-rings shared.
POEM	
POEM	40. His messengers went | by the ways so wet,
POEM	And came to the hall | where Hersir dwelt;
POEM	His daughter was fair | and slender-fingered,
POEM	Erna the wise | the maiden was.
POEM	
POEM	41. Her hand they sought, | and home they brought her,
POEM	Wedded to Jarl | the veil she wore;
POEM	Together they dwelt, | their joy was great,
POEM	Children they had, | and happy they lived.
POEM	
POEM	42. Bur was the eldest, | and Barn the next,
POEM	Joth and Athal, | Arfi, Mog,
POEM	Nith and Svein, | soon they began-
POEM	Sun and Nithjung-- | to play and swim;
POEM	Kund was one, | and the youngest Kon.
POEM	
POEM	43. Soon grew up | the sons of Jarl,
POEM	Beasts they tamed, | and bucklers rounded,
POEM	Shafts they fashioned, | and spears they shook.
POEM	
POEM	44. But Kon the Young | learned runes to use,
POEM	Runes everlasting, | the runes of life;
POEM	Soon could he well | the warriors shield,
POEM	Dull the swordblade, | and still the seas.
POEM	
POEM	45. Bird-chatter learned he, | flames could he lessen.,
POEM	Minds could quiet, | and sorrows calm;
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	The might and strength | of twice four men.
POEM	
POEM	46. With Rig-Jarl soon | the runes he shared,
POEM	More crafty he was, | and greater his wisdom;
POEM	The right he sought, | and soon he won it,
POEM	Rig to be called, | and runes to know.
POEM	
POEM	47. Young Kon rode forth | through forest and grove,
POEM	Shafts let loose, | and birds he lured;
POEM	
POEM	There spake a crow | on a bough that sat:
POEM	Why lurest thou, Kon, | the birds to come?
POEM	
POEM	48.  'Twere better forth | on thy steed to fare,
POEM	. . . . . | and the host to slay.
POEM	
POEM	49. "The halls of Dan | and Danp are noble,
POEM	Greater their wealth | than thou bast gained;
POEM	Good are they | at guiding the keel,
POEM	Trying of weapons, | and giving of wounds.
TITLE	HYNDLULJOTH
SUBTITLE	The Poem of Hyndla
POEM	1. "Maiden, awake! | wake thee, my friend,
POEM	My sister Hyndla, | in thy hollow cave!
POEM	Already comes darkness, | and ride must we
POEM	To Valhall to seek | the sacred hall.
POEM	
POEM	2. "The favor of Heerfather | seek we to find,
POEM	To his followers gold | he gladly gives;
POEM	To Hermoth gave he | helm and mail-coat,
POEM	And to Sigmund he gave | a sword as gift.
POEM	
POEM	3. "Triumph to some, | and treasure to others,
POEM	To many wisdom | and skill in words,
POEM	Fair winds to the sailor, | to the singer his art,
POEM	And a manly heart | to many a hero.
POEM	
POEM	4. "Thor shall I honor, | and this shall I ask,
POEM	That his favor true | mayst thou ever find;
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Though little the brides | of the giants he loves.
POEM	
POEM	5. "From the stall now | one of thy wolves lead forth,
POEM	And along with my boar | shalt thou let him run;
POEM	For slow my boar goes | on the road of the gods,
POEM	And I would not weary | my worthy steed."
POEM	
POEM	Hyndla spake:
POEM	6. "Falsely thou askest me, | Freyja, to go,
POEM	For so in the glance | of thine eyes I see;
POEM	On the way of the slain | thy lover goes with thee.
POEM	Ottar the young, | the son of Instein."
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	7. "Wild dreams, methinks, | are thine when thou sayest
POEM	My lover is with me | on the way of the slain;
POEM	There shines the boar | with bristles of gold,
POEM	Hildisvini, | he who was made
POEM	By Dain and Nabbi, | the cunning dwarfs.
POEM	
POEM	8. "Now let us down | from our saddles leap,
POEM	And talk of the race | of the heroes twain;
POEM	The men who were born | of the gods above,
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	9. "A wager have made | in the foreign metal
POEM	Ottar the young | and Angantyr;
POEM	We must guard, for the hero | young to have,
POEM	His father's wealth, | the fruits of his race.
POEM	
POEM	10. "For me a shrine | of stones he made,--
POEM	And now to glass | the rock has grown;--
POEM	Oft with the blood | of beasts was it red;
POEM	In the goddesses ever | did Ottar trust.
POEM	
POEM	11. "Tell to me now | the ancient names,
POEM	And the races of all | that were born of old:
POEM	Who are of the Skjoldungs, | who of the Skilfings,
POEM	Who of the Othlings, | who of the Ylfings,
POEM	Who are the free-born, | who are the high-born,
POEM	The noblest of men | that in Mithgarth dwell?"
POEM	
POEM	Hyndla spake:
POEM	12. "Thou art, Ottar, | the son of Instein,
POEM	And Instein the son | of Alf the Old,
POEM	Alf of Ulf, | Ulf of Sæfari,
POEM	And Sæfari's father | was Svan the Red.
POEM	
POEM	13. "Thy mother, bright | with bracelets fair,
POEM	Hight, methinks, | the priestess Hledis;
POEM	Frothi her father, | and Friaut her mother;--
POEM	Her race of the mightiest | men must seem.
POEM	
POEM	14. "Of old the noblest | of all was Ali,
POEM	Before him Halfdan, | foremost of Skjoldungs;
POEM	Famed were the battles | the hero fought,
POEM	To the corners of heaven | his deeds were carried.
POEM	
POEM	15. "Strengthened by Eymund, | the strongest of men,
POEM	Sigtrygg he slew | with the ice-cold sword;
POEM	His bride was Almveig, | the best of women,
POEM	And eighteen boys | did Almveig bear him.
POEM	
POEM	16. "Hence come the Skjoldungs, | hence the Skilfings,
POEM	Hence the Othlings, | hence the Ynglings,
POEM	Hence come the free-born, | hence the high-born,
POEM	The noblest of men | that in Mithgarth dwell:
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	17. "Hildigun then | her mother hight,
POEM	The daughter of Svava | and Sækonung;
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	It is much to know,-- | wilt thou hear yet more?
POEM	
POEM	18. "The mate of Dag | was a mother of heroes,
POEM	Thora, who bore him | the bravest of fighters,
POEM	Frathmar and Gyrth | and the Frekis twain,
POEM	Am and Jofurmar, | Alf the Old;
POEM	It is much to know,-- | wilt thou hear yet more?
POEM	
POEM	19. "Her husband was Ketil, | the heir of Klypp,
POEM	He was of thy mother | the mother's-father;
POEM	Before the days | of Kari was Frothi,
POEM	And horn of Hild | was Hoalf then.
POEM	
POEM	20. "Next was Nanna, | daughter of Nokkvi,
POEM	Thy father's kinsman | her son became;
POEM	Old is the line, | and longer still,
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	21. "Isolf and Osolf, | the sons of Olmoth,
POEM	Whose wife was Skurhild, | the daughter of Skekkil,
POEM	Count them among | the heroes mighty,
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	22. "Gunnar the Bulwark, | Grim the Hardy,
POEM	Thorir the Iron-shield, | Ulf the Gaper,
POEM	Brodd and Hörvir | both did I know;
POEM	In the household they were | of Hrolf the Old.
POEM	
POEM	23. "Hervarth, Hjorvarth, | Hrani, Angantyr,
POEM	Bui and Brami, | Barri and Reifnir,
POEM	Tind and Tyrfing, | the Haddings twain,--
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	24. "Eastward in Bolm | were born of old
POEM	The sons of Arngrim | and Eyfura;
POEM	With berserk-tumult | and baleful deed
POEM	Like fire o'er land | and sea they fared,
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	25. "The sons of Jormunrek | all of yore
POEM	To the gods in death | were as offerings given;
POEM	He was kinsman of Sigurth,-- | hear well what I say,--
POEM	The foe of hosts, | and Fafnir's slayer.
POEM	
POEM	26., "From Volsung's seed | was the hero sprung,
POEM	And Hjordis was born | of Hrauthung's race,
POEM	And Eylimi | from the Othlings came,--
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	27. "Gunnar and Hogni, | the heirs of Gjuki,
POEM	And Guthrun as well, | who their sister was;
POEM	But Gotthorm was not | of Gjuki's race,
POEM	Although the brother | of both he was:
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!
POEM	
POEM	28. "Of Hvethna's sons | was Haki the best,
POEM	And Hjorvarth the father | of Hvethna was;
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	29. "Harald Battle-tooth | of Auth was born,
POEM	Hrörek the Ring-giver | her husband was;
POEM	Auth the Deep-minded | was Ivar's daughter,
POEM	But Rathbarth the father | of Randver was:
POEM	And all are thy kinsmen, | Ottar, thou fool!"
POEM	* * *
POEM	Fragment of "The Short Voluspo"
POEM	
POEM	30. Eleven in number | the gods were known,
POEM	When Baldr o'er the hill | of death was bowed;
POEM	And this to avenge | was Vali swift,
POEM	When his brother's slayer | soon he slew.
POEM	
POEM	31. The father of Baldr | was the heir of Bur,
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	32. Freyr's wife was Gerth, | the daughter of Gymir,
POEM	Of the giants' brood, | and Aurbotha bore her;
POEM	To these as well | was Thjazi kin,
POEM	The dark-loving giant; | his daughter was Skathi.
POEM	
POEM	33. Much have I told thee, | and further will tell;
POEM	There is much that I know;-- | wilt thou hear yet more?
POEM	
POEM	34. Heith and Hrossthjof, | the children of Hrimnir.
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	35. The sybils arose | from Vitholf's race,
POEM	From Vilmeith all | the seers are,
POEM	And the workers of charms | are Svarthofthi's children,
POEM	And from Ymir sprang | the giants all.
POEM	
POEM	36. Much have I told thee, | and further will tell;
POEM	There is much that I know;-- | wilt thou hear yet more?
POEM	
POEM	37. One there was born | in the bygone days,
POEM	Of the race of the gods, | and great was his might;
POEM	Nine giant women, | at the world's edge,
POEM	Once bore the man | so mighty in arms.
POEM	
POEM	38. Gjolp there bore him, | Greip there bore him,
POEM	Eistla bore him, | and Eyrgjafa,
POEM	Ulfrun bore him, | and Angeyja,
POEM	Imth and Atla, | and Jarnsaxa.
POEM	
POEM	39. Strong was he made | with the strength of earth,
POEM	With the ice-cold sea, | and the blood of swine.
POEM	
POEM	40. One there was born, | the best of all,
POEM	And strong was he made | with the strength of earth;
POEM	The proudest is called | the kinsman of men
POEM	Of the rulers all | throughout the world.
POEM	
POEM	41. Much have I told thee, | and further will tell;
POEM	There is much that I know;-- | wilt thou hear yet more?
POEM	
POEM	42. The wolf did Loki | with Angrbotha win,
POEM	And Sleipnir bore he | to Svathilfari;
POEM	The worst of marvels | seemed the one
POEM	That sprang from the brother | of Byleist then.
POEM	
POEM	43. A heart ate Loki,-- | in the embers it lay,
POEM	And half-cooked found he | the woman's heart;--
POEM	With child from the woman | Lopt soon was,
POEM	And thence among men | came the monsters all.
POEM	
POEM	44. The sea, storm-driven, | seeks heaven itself,
POEM	O'er the earth it flows, | the air grows sterile;
POEM	Then follow the snows | and the furious winds,
POEM	For the gods are doomed, | and the end is death.
POEM	
POEM	45. Then comes another, | a greater than all,
POEM	Though never I dare | his name to speak;
POEM	Few are they now | that farther can see
POEM	Than the moment when Othin | shall meet the wolf.
POEM	* * *
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	46. "To my boar now bring | the memory-beer,
POEM	So that all thy words, | that well thou hast spoken,
POEM	The third morn hence | he may hold in mind,
POEM	When their races Ottar | and Angantyr tell."
POEM	
POEM	Hyndla spake:
POEM	47. "Hence shalt thou fare, | for fain would I sleep,
POEM	From me thou gettest | few favors good;
POEM	My noble one, out | in the night thou leapest
POEM	As. Heithrun goes | the goats among.
POEM	
POEM	48. "To Oth didst thou run, | who loved thee ever,
POEM	And many under | thy apron have crawled;
POEM	My noble one, out | in the night thou leapest,
POEM	As Heithrun goes | the goats among."
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	49. "Around the giantess | flames shall I raise,
POEM	So that forth unburned | thou mayst not fare."
POEM	
POEM	Hyndla spake:
POEM	50. "Flames I see burning, | the earth is on fire,
POEM	And each for his life | the price must lose;
POEM	Bring then to Ottar | the draught of beer,
POEM	Of venom full | for an evil fate."
POEM	
POEM	Freyja spake:
POEM	51. "Thine evil words | shall work no ill,
POEM	Though, giantess, bitter | thy baleful threats;
POEM	A drink full fair | shall Ottar find,
POEM	If of all the gods | the favor I get."
TITLE	SVIPDAGSMOL
SUBTITLE	The Ballad of Svipdag
POEM	1. "Wake thee, Groa! | wake, mother good!
POEM	At the doors of the dead I call thee;
POEM	Thy son, bethink thee, | thou badst to seek
POEM	Thy help at the hill of death."
POEM	
POEM	Groa spake:
POEM	2. "What evil vexes | mine only son,
POEM	What baleful fate hast thou found,
POEM	That thou callest thy mother, | who lies in the mould,
POEM	And the world of the living has left?"
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	3. "The woman false | whom my father embraced
POEM	Has brought me a baleful game;
POEM	For she bade me go forth | where none may fare,
POEM	And Mengloth the maid to seek."
POEM	
POEM	Groa spake:
POEM	4. "Long is the way, | long must thou wander,
POEM	But long is love as well;
POEM	Thou mayst find, perchance, | what thou fain wouldst have,
POEM	If the fates their favor will give."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	5. "Charms full good | then chant to me, mother,
POEM	And seek thy son to guard;
POEM	For death do I fear | on the way I shall fare,
POEM	And in years am I young, methinks."
POEM	
POEM	Groa spake:
POEM	6. "Then first I will chant thee | the charm oft-tried,
POEM	That Rani taught to Rind;
POEM	From the shoulder whate'er | mislikes thee shake,
POEM	For helper thyself shalt thou have.
POEM	
POEM	7. "Then next I will chant thee, | if needs thou must travel,
POEM	And wander a purposeless way:
POEM	The bolts of Urth | shall on every side
POEM	Be thy guards on the road thou goest.
POEM	
POEM	8. "Then third I will chant thee, | if threatening streams
POEM	The danger of death shall bring:
POEM	Yet to Hel shall turn | both Horn and Ruth,
POEM	And before thee the waters shall fail.
POEM	
POEM	9. "Then fourth I will chant thee, | if come thy foes
POEM	On the gallows-way against thee:
POEM	Into thine hands | shall their hearts be given,
POEM	And peace shall the warriors wish.
POEM	
POEM	10. "Then fifth I will chant thee, | if fetters perchance
POEM	Shall bind thy bending limbs:
POEM	O'er thy thighs do I chant | a loosening-charm,
POEM	And the lock is burst from the limbs,
POEM	And the fetters fall from the feet.
POEM	
POEM	11. "Then sixth I will chant thee, | if storms on the sea
POEM	Have might unknown to man:
POEM	Yet never shall wind | or wave do harm,
POEM	And calm is the course of thy boat.
POEM	
POEM	12. "Then seventh I chant thee, | if frost shall seek
POEM	To kill thee on lofty crags:
POEM	The fatal cold | shall not grip thy flesh,
POEM	And whole thy body shall be.
POEM	
POEM	13. "Then eighth will I chant thee, | if ever by night
POEM	Thou shalt wander on murky ways:
POEM	Yet never the curse | of a Christian woman
POEM	From the dead shall do thee harm.
POEM	
POEM	14. "Then ninth will I chant thee, | if needs thou must strive
POEM	With a warlike giant in words:
POEM	Thy heart good store | of wit shall have,
POEM	And thy mouth of words full wise.
POEM	
POEM	15. "Now fare on the way | where danger waits,
POEM	Let evils not lessen thy love!
POEM	I have stood at the door | of the earth-fixed stones,
POEM	The while I chanted thee charms.
POEM	
POEM	16. "Bear hence, my son, | what thy mother hath said,
POEM	And let it live in thy breast;
POEM	Thine ever shall be the | best of fortune,
POEM	So long as my words shall last."
POEM	II. FJOLMINNSMOL
POEM	THE LAY OF FJOLSVITH
POEM	
POEM	17. Before the house | he beheld one coming
POEM	To the home of the giants high.
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	What giant is here, | in front of the house,
POEM	And around him fires are flaming?
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	3. "What seekest thou here? | for what is thy search?
POEM	What, friendless one, fain wouldst thou know?
POEM	By the ways so wet | must thou wander hence,
POEM	For, weakling, no home hast thou here."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	19. "What giant is here, | in front of the house,
POEM	To the wayfarer welcome denying?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	Greeting full fair | thou never shalt find,
POEM	So hence shalt thou get thee home.
POEM	
POEM	20. Fjolsvith am I, | and wise am I found,
POEM	But miserly am I with meat;
POEM	Thou never shalt enter | within the house,--
POEM	Go forth like a wolf on thy way!"
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	21. "Few from the joy | of their eyes will go forth,
POEM	When the sight of their loves they seek;
POEM	Full bright are the gates | of the golden hall,
POEM	And a home shall I here enjoy."
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	22. "Tell me now, fellow, | what father thou hast,
POEM	And the kindred of whom thou camst."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	Vindkald am I, | and Varkald's son,
POEM	And Fjolkald his father was.
POEM	
POEM	23. Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	Who is it that holds | and has for his own
POEM	The rule of the hall so rich?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	224. "Mengloth is she, | her mother bore her
POEM	To the son of Svafrthorin;
POEM	She is it that holds | and has for her own
POEM	The rule of the hall so rich."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	25. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the gate? | for among the gods
POEM	Ne'er saw man so grim a sight."
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	26. "Thrymgjol they call it; | 'twas made by the three,
POEM	The sons of Solblindi;
POEM	And fast as a fetter | the farer it holds,
POEM	Whoever shall lift the latch."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	27. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the house? | for no man beheld
POEM	Mongst the gods so grim a sight."
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	28. "Gastropnir is it, | of old I made it
POEM	From the limbs of Leirbrimir;
POEM	I braced it so strongly | that fast it shall stand
POEM	So long as the world shall last."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	29. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the tree | that casts abroad
POEM	Its limbs o'er every land?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	30. "Mimameith its name, | and no man knows
POEM	What root beneath it runs;
POEM	And few can guess | what shall fell the tree,
POEM	For fire nor iron shall fell it."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	31. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What grows from the seed | of the tree so great,
POEM	That fire nor iron shall fell?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	32. "Women, sick | with child, shall seek
POEM	Its fruit to the flames to bear;
POEM	Then out shall come | what within was hid,
POEM	And so is it mighty with men."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	33. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What cock is he | on the highest bough,
POEM	That glitters all with gold?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	34. "Vithofnir his name, | and now he shines
POEM	Like lightning on Mimameith's limbs;
POEM	And great is the trouble | with which he grieves
POEM	Both Surt and Sinmora."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	35. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the hounds, | that before the house
POEM	So fierce and angry are?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	36. "Gif call they one, | and Geri the other,
POEM	If now the truth thou wouldst know;
POEM	Great they are, | and their might will grow,
POEM	Till the gods to death are doomed."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	37. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	May no man hope | the house to enter,
POEM	While the hungry hounds are sleeping?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	38. "Together they sleep not, | for so was it fixed
POEM	When the guard to them was given;
POEM	One sleeps by night, | the next by day,
POEM	So no man may enter ever."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	39, "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	Is there no meat | that men may give them,
POEM	And leap within while they eat?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	40. "Two wing-joints there be | in Vithofnir's body,
POEM	If now the truth thou wouldst know;
POEM	That alone is the meat | that men may give them,
POEM	And leap within while they eat."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	41. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What weapon can send | Vithofnir to seek
POEM	The house of Hel below?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	42. "Lævatein is there, | that Lopt with runes
POEM	Once made by the doors of death;
POEM	In Lægjarn's chest | by Sinmora lies it,
POEM	And nine locks fasten it firm."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	43. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	May a man come thence, | who thither goes,
POEM	And tries the sword to take?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	44. "Thence may he come | who thither goes,
POEM	And tries the sword to take,
POEM	If with him he carries | what few can win,
POEM	To give to the goddess of gold."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	45. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What treasure is there | that men may take
POEM	To rejoice the giantess pale?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	46. "The sickle bright | in thy wallet bear,
POEM	Mid Vithofnir's feathers found;
POEM	To Sinmora give it, | and then shall she grant
POEM	That the weapon by thee be won."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	47. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the hall, | encompassed here
POEM	With flickering magic flames?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	48. "Lyr is it called, | and long it shall
POEM	On the tip of a spear-point tremble;
POEM	Of the noble house | mankind has heard,
POEM	But more has it never known."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	49. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What one of the gods | has made so great
POEM	The hall I behold within?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	50. "Uni and Iri, | Bari and Jari,
POEM	Var and Vegdrasil,
POEM	Dori and Ori, | Delling, and there
POEM	Was Loki, the fear of the folk."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	51. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What call they the mountain | on which the maid
POEM	Is lying so lovely to see?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	52. "Lyfjaberg is it, | and long shall it be
POEM	A joy to the sick and the sore;
POEM	For well shall grow | each woman who climbs it,
POEM	Though sick full long she has lain."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	53. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	What maidens are they | that at Mengloth's knees
POEM	Are sitting so gladly together?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	54. "Hlif is one named, | Hlifthrasa another,
POEM	Thjothvara call they the third;
POEM	Bjort and Bleik, | Blith and Frith,
POEM	Eir and Aurbotha."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	55. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	Aid bring they to all | who offerings give,
POEM	If need be found therefor?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	56. "Soon aid they all | who offerings give
POEM	On the holy altars high;
POEM	And if danger they see | for the sons of men,
POEM	Then each from ill do they guard."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	57. "Now answer me, Fjolsvith, | the question I ask,
POEM	For now the truth would I know:
POEM	Lives there the man | who in Mengloth's arms
POEM	So fair may seek to sleep?"
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	58. "No man there is | who in Mengloth's arms
POEM	So fair may seek to sleep,
POEM	Save Svipdag alone, | for the sun-bright maid
POEM	Is destined his bride to be."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	59. "Fling back the gates! | make the gateway wide!
POEM	Here mayst thou Svipdag see!
POEM	Hence get thee to find | if gladness soon
POEM	Mengloth to me will give."
POEM	
POEM	Fjolsvith spake:
POEM	60. "Hearken, Mengloth, | a man is come;
POEM	Go thou the guest to see!
POEM	The hounds are fawning, | the house bursts open,--
POEM	Svipdag, methinks, is there."
POEM	
POEM	Mengloth spake:
POEM	61. "On the gallows high | shall hungry ravens
POEM	Soon thine eyes pluck out,
POEM	If thou liest in saying | that here at last
POEM	The hero is come to my hall.
POEM	
POEM	62. "Whence camest thou hither? | how camest thou here?
POEM	What name do thy kinsmen call thee?
POEM	Thy race and thy name | as a sign must I know,
POEM	That thy bride I am destined to be."
POEM	
POEM	Svipdag spake:
POEM	63. "Svipdag am I, | and Solbjart's son;
POEM	Thence came I by wind-cold ways;
POEM	With the words of Urth | shall no man war,
POEM	Though unearned her gifts be given."
POEM	
POEM	Mengloth spake:
POEM	64. "Welcome thou art, | for long have I waited;
POEM	The welcoming kiss shalt thou win!
POEM	For two who love | is the longed-for meeting
POEM	The greatest gladness of all.
POEM	
POEM	65. "Long have I sat | on Lyfjaberg here,
POEM	Awaiting thee day by day;
POEM	And now I have | what I ever hoped,
POEM	For here thou art come to my hall.
POEM	
POEM	66. "Alike we yearned; | I longed for thee,
POEM	And thou for my love hast longed;
POEM	But now henceforth | together we know
POEM	Our lives to the end we shall live."
TITLE	VÖLUNDARKVITHA
SUBTITLE	The Lay of Völund
POEM	1. Maids from the south | through Myrkwood flew,
POEM	Fair and young, | their fate to follow;
POEM	On the shore of the sea | to rest them they sat,
POEM	The maids of the south, | and flax they spun.
POEM	
POEM	2. . . . . . . . . . .
POEM	Hlathguth and Hervor, | Hlothver's children,
POEM	And Olrun the Wise | Kjar's daughter was.
POEM	
POEM	3. . . . . . . . . . .
POEM	One in her arms | took Egil then
POEM	To her bosom white, | the woman fair.
POEM	
POEM	4. Swan-White second,-- | swan-feathers she wore,
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	And her arms the third | of the sisters threw
POEM	Next round Völund's | neck so white.
POEM	
POEM	5. There did they sit | for seven winters,
POEM	In the eighth at last | came their longing again,
POEM	(And in the ninth | did need divide them).
POEM	The maidens yearned | for the murky wood,
POEM	The fair young maids, | their fate to follow.
POEM	
POEM	6. Völund home | from his hunting came,
POEM	From a weary way, | the weather-wise bowman,
POEM	Slagfith and Egil | the hall found empty,
POEM	Out and in went they, | everywhere seeking.
POEM	
POEM	7. East fared Egil | after Olrun,
