POEM	All fearless she went, | and the guests did she welcome;
POEM	To the Niflungs she went-- | her last greeting it was,--
POEM	In her speech truth was clear, | and much would she speak.
POEM	
POEM	45. "For your safety I sought | that at home ye should stay;
POEM	None escapes his fate, | so ye hither must fare."
POEM	Full wisely she spake, | if yet peace they might win,
POEM	But to nought would they hearken, | and "No" said they all.
POEM	
POEM	46. Then the high-born one saw | that hard was their battle,
POEM	In fierceness of heart | she flung off her mantle;
POEM	Her naked sword grasped she | her kin's lives to guard,
POEM	Not gentle her hands | in the hewing of battle.
POEM	
POEM	47. Then the daughter of Gjuki | two warriors smote down,
POEM	Atli's brother she slew, | and forth then they bore him;
POEM	(So fiercely she fought | that his feet she clove off;)
POEM	Another she smote | so that never he stood,
POEM	To hell did she send him,-- | her hands trembled never.
POEM	
POEM	48. Full wide was the fame | of the battle they fought,
POEM	Twas the greatest of deeds | of the sons of Gjuki;
POEM	Men say that the Niflungs, | while themselves they were living,
POEM	With their swords fought mightily, | mail-coats they sundered,
POEM	And helms did they hew, | as their hearts were fearless.
POEM	
POEM	49. All the morning they fought | until midday shone,
POEM	(All the dusk as well | and the dawning of day,)
POEM	When the battle was ended, | the field flowed with blood;
POEM	Ere they fell, eighteen | of their foemen were slain,
POEM	By the two sons of Bera | and her brother as well.
POEM	
POEM	50. Then the warrior spake, | and wild was his anger:
POEM	This is evil to see, | and thy doing is all;
POEM	Once we were thirty, | we thanes, keen for battle,
POEM	Now eleven are left, | and great is our lack.
POEM	
POEM	51. There were five of us brothers | when Buthli we lost,
POEM	Now Hel has the half, | and two smitten lie here;
POEM	A great kinship had I,-- | the truth may I hide not,--
POEM	From a wife bringing slaughter | small joy could I win.
POEM	
POEM	52. We lay seldom together | since to me thou wast given,
POEM	Now my kin all are gone, | of my gold am I robbed;
POEM	Nay, and worst, thou didst send | my sister to hell."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	53. "Hear me now, Atli! | the first evil was thine;
POEM	My mother didst thou take, | and for gold didst murder her,
POEM	My sister's daughter | thou didst starve in a prison.
POEM	A jest does it seem | that thy sorrow thou tellest,
POEM	And good do I find it | that grief to thee comes."
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	54. "Go now, ye warriors, | and make greater the grief
POEM	Of the woman so fair, | for fain would I see it;
POEM	So fierce be thy warring | that Guthrun shall weep,
POEM	I would gladly behold | her happiness lost.
POEM	
POEM	55. "Seize ye now Hogni, | and with knives shall ye hew him,
POEM	His heart shall ye cut out, | this haste ye to do;
POEM	And grim-hearted Gunnar | shall ye bind on the gallows,
POEM	Swift shall ye do it, | to serpents now cast him."
POEM	
POEM	Hogni spake:
POEM	56. "Do now as thou wilt, | for glad I await it,
POEM	Brave shalt thou find me, | I have faced worse before;
POEM	We held thee at bay | while whole we were fighting,
POEM	Now with wounds are we spent, | so thy will canst thou work."
POEM	
POEM	57. Then did Beiti speak, | he was Atli's steward:
POEM	Let us seize now Hjalli, | and Hogni spare we!
POEM	Let us fell the sluggard, | he is fit for death,
POEM	He has lived too long, | and lazy men call him.
POEM	
POEM	58. Afraid was the pot-watcher, | he fled here and yon,
POEM	And crazed with his terror | he climbed in the corners:
POEM	Ill for me is this fighting, | if I pay for your fierceness,
POEM	And sad is the day | to die leaving my swine
POEM	And all the fair victuals | that of old did I have.
POEM	
POEM	59. They seized Buthli's cook, | and they came with the knife,
POEM	The frightened thrall howled | ere the edge did he feel;
POEM	He was willing, he cried, | to dung well the court yard,
POEM	Do the basest of work, | if spare him they would;
POEM	Full happy were Hjalli | if his life he might have.
POEM	
POEM	60. Then fain was Hogni-- | there are few would do thus--
POEM	To beg for the slave | that safe hence he should go;
POEM	I would find it far better | this knife-play to feel,
POEM	Why must we all hark | to this howling longer?
POEM	
POEM	61. Then the brave one they seized; | to the warriors bold
POEM	No chance was there left | to delay his fate longer;
POEM	Loud did Hogni laugh, | all the sons of day heard him,
POEM	So valiant he was | that well he could suffer.
POEM	* * * * * *
POEM	
POEM	62. A harp Gunnar seized, | with his toes he smote it
POEM	So well did he strike | that the women all wept,
POEM	And the men, when clear | they heard it, lamented;
POEM	Full noble was his song, | the rafters burst asunder.
POEM	
POEM	63. Then the heroes died | ere the day was yet come;
POEM	Their fame did they leave | ever lofty to live.
POEM	. . . . . . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	64. Full mighty seemed Atli | as o'er them he stood,
POEM	The wise one he blamed, | and his words reproached her:
POEM	It is morning, Guthrun; | now thy dear ones dost miss,
POEM	But the blame is part thine | that thus it has chanced.
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	65. "Thou art joyous, Atli, | for of evil thou tellest,
POEM	But sorrow is thine | if thou mightest all see;
POEM	Thy heritage heavy | here can I tell thee,
POEM	Sorrow never thou losest | unless I shall die."
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	66. "Not free of guilt am I; | a way shall I find
POEM	That is better by far,-- | oft the fairest we shunned;--
POEM	With slaves I console thee, | with gems fair to see,
POEM	And with silver snow-white, | as thyself thou shalt choose."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	67. "No hope shall this give thee, | thy gifts I shall take not,
POEM	Requital I spurned | when my sorrows were smaller;
POEM	Once grim did I seem, | but now greater my grimness,
POEM	There was nought seemed too hard | while Hogni was living.
POEM	
POEM	68. "Our childhood did we have | in a single house,
POEM	We played many a game, | in the grove did we grow;
POEM	Then did Grimhild give us | gold and necklaces,
POEM	Thou shalt ne'er make amends | for my brother's murder,
POEM	Nor ever shalt win me | to think it was well.
POEM	
POEM	69. "But the fierceness of men | rules the fate of women,
POEM	The tree-top bows low | if bereft of its leaves,
POEM	The tree bends over | if the roots are cleft under it;
POEM	Now mayest thou, Atli, | o'er all things here rule."
POEM	
POEM	70. Full heedless the warrior | was that he trusted her,
POEM	So clear was her guile | if on guard he had been;
POEM	But crafty was Guthrun, | with cunning she spake,
POEM	Her glance she made pleasant, | with two shields she played.
POEM	
POEM	71. The beer then she brought | for her brothers' death feast,
POEM	And a feast Atli made | for his followers dead
POEM	No more did they speak, | the mead was made ready,
POEM	Soon the men were gathered | with mighty uproar.
POEM	
POEM	72. Thus bitterly planned she, | and Buthli's race threatened,
POEM	And terrible vengeance | on her husband would take;
POEM	The little ones called she, | on a block she laid them;
POEM	Afraid were the proud ones, | but their tears did not fall;
POEM	To their mother's arms went they, | and asked what she would.
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	73. "Nay, ask me no more! | You both shall I murder,
POEM	For long have I wished | your lives to steal from you.
POEM	
POEM	The boys spake:
POEM	Slay thy boys as thou wilt, | for no one may bar it,
POEM	Short the angry one's peace | if all thou shalt do.
POEM	
POEM	74. Then the grim one slew both | of the brothers young,
POEM	Full hard was her deed | when their heads she smote off;
POEM	Fain was Atli to know | whither now they were gone,
POEM	The boys from their sport, | for nowhere he spied them.
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	75. "My fate shall I seek, | all to Atli saying,
POEM	The daughter of Grimhild | the deed from thee hides not;
POEM	No joy thou hast, Atli, | if all thou shalt hear,
POEM	Great sorrow didst wake | when my brothers thou slewest.
POEM	
POEM	76. '1 have seldom slept | since the hour they were slain,
POEM	Baleful were my threats, | now I bid thee recall them;
POEM	Thou didst say it was morning,-- | too well I remember,--
POEM	Now is evening come, | and this question thou askest.
POEM	
POEM	77. "Now both of thy sons | thou hast lost . . . .
POEM	. . . . . | as thou never shouldst do;
POEM	The skulls of thy boys | thou as beer-cups didst have,
POEM	And the draught that I made thee | was mixed with their blood.
POEM	
POEM	78. 'I cut out their hearts, | on a spit I cooked them,
POEM	I came to thee with them, | and calf's flesh I called them;
POEM	Alone didst thou eat them, | nor any didst leave,
POEM	Thou didst greedily bite, | and thy teeth were busy.
POEM	
POEM	79. "Of thy sons now thou knowest; | few suffer more sorrow;
POEM	My guilt have I told, | fame it never shall give me."
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	80. "Grim wast thou, Guthrun, | in so grievous a deed,
POEM	My draught with the blood | of thy boys to mingle;
POEM	Thou hast slain thine own kin, | most ill it be seemed thee,
POEM	And little for me | twixt my sorrows thou leavest."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	81. "Still more would I seek | to slay thee thyself,
POEM	Enough ill comes seldom | to such as thou art;
POEM	Thou didst folly of old, | such that no one shall find
POEM	In the whole world of men | a match for such madness.
POEM	Now this that of late | we learned hast thou added,
POEM	Great evil hast grasped, | and thine own death feast made."
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	82. "With fire shall they burn thee, | and first shall they stone thee,
POEM	So then hast thou earned | what thou ever hast sought for."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	Such woes for thyself | shalt thou say in the morning,
POEM	From a finer death I | to another light fare.
POEM	
POEM	83. Together they sat | and full grim were their thoughts,
POEM	Unfriendly their words, | and no joy either found;
POEM	In Hniflung grew hatred, | great plans did he have,
POEM	To Guthrun his anger | against Atli was told.
POEM	
POEM	84. To her heart came ever | the fate of Hogni,
POEM	She told him 'twere well | if he vengeance should win;
POEM	So was Atli slain,-- | 'twas not slow to await,--
POEM	Hogni's son slew him, | and Guthrun herself.
POEM	
POEM	85. Then the warrior spake, | as from slumber he wakened,
POEM	Soon he knew for his wounds | would the bandage do nought:
POEM	Now the truth shalt thou say: | who has slain Buthli's son?
POEM	Full sore am I smitten, | nor hope can I see.
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	86. "Ne'er her deed from thee hides | the daughter of Grimhild,
POEM	I own to the guilt | that is ending thy life,
POEM	And the son of Hogni; | 'tis so thy wounds bleed."
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	To murder hast thou fared, | though foul it must seem;
POEM	Ill thy friend to betray | who trusted thee well.
POEM	
POEM	87. Not glad went I hence | thy hand to seek, Guthrun,
POEM	In thy widowhood famed, | but haughty men found thee;
POEM	My belief did not lie, | as now we have learned;
POEM	I brought thee home hither, | and a host of men with us.
POEM	
POEM	88. "Most noble was all | when of old we journeyed,
POEM	Great honor did we have | of heroes full worthy;
POEM	Of cattle had we plenty, | and greatly we prospered,
POEM	Mighty was our wealth, | and many received it.
POEM	
POEM	89. "To the famed one as bride-gift | I gave jewels fair,
POEM	I gave thirty slaves, | and handmaidens seven;
POEM	There was honor in such gifts, | yet the silver was greater.
POEM	
POEM	90. "But all to thee was | as if nought it were worth,
POEM	While the land lay before thee | that Buthli had left me;
POEM	Thou in secret didst work | so the treasure I won not;
POEM	My mother full oft | to sit weeping didst make,
POEM	No wedded joy found I | in fullness of heart."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	91. "Thou liest now, Atli, | though little I heed it;
POEM	If I seldom was kindly, | full cruel wast thou;
POEM	Ye brothers fought young, | quarrels brought you to battle,
POEM	And half went to hell | of the sons of thy house,
POEM	And all was destroyed | that should e'er have done good.
POEM	
POEM	92. "My two brothers and I | were bold in our thoughts,
POEM	From the land we went forth, | with Sigurth we fared;
POEM	Full swiftly we sailed, | each one steering his ship,
POEM	So our fate sought we e'er | till we came to the East.
POEM	
POEM	93. "First the king did we slay, | and the land we seized,
POEM	The princes did us service, | for such was their fear;
POEM	From the forest we called | them we fain would have guiltless,
POEM	And rich made we many | who of all were bereft.
POEM	
POEM	94. "Slain was the Hun-king, | soon happiness vanished,
POEM	In her grief the widow | so young sat weeping;
POEM	Yet worse seemed the sorrow | to seek Atli's house,
POEM	A hero was my husband, | and hard was his loss.
POEM	
POEM	95. "From the Thing thou camst never, | for thus have we heard,
POEM	Having won in thy quarrels, | or warriors smitten;
POEM	Full yielding thou wast, | never firm was thy will,
POEM	In silence didst suffer, | . . . . .
POEM	
POEM	Atli spake:
POEM	96. "Thou liest now, Guthrun, | but little of good
POEM	Will it bring to either, | for all have we lost;
POEM	But, Guthrun, yet once | be thou kindly of will,
POEM	For the honor of both, | when forth I am home."
POEM	
POEM	Guthrun spake:
POEM	97. "A ship will I buy, | and a bright-hued coffin,
POEM	I will wax well the shroud | to wind round thy body,
POEM	For all will I care | as if dear were we ever."
POEM	
POEM	98. Then did Atli die, | and his heirs' grief doubled;
POEM	The high-born one did | as to him she had promised;
POEM	Then sought Guthrun the wise | to go to her death,
POEM	But for days did she wait, | and 'twas long ere she died.
POEM	
POEM	99. Full happy shall he be | who such offspring has,
POEM	Or children so gallant, | as Gjuki begot;
POEM	Forever shall live, | and in lands far and wide,
POEM	Their valor heroic | wherever men hear it.
